Account	Security contact information should be provided for an AWS account	Compliance	High	Security contact information should be provided for an AWS account. Steps: 1. Navigate to the AWS Management Console. 2. Update the security contact information under the account settings. https://docs.aws.amazon.com/accounts/latest/reference/account-settings.html	$0 (no additional cost)

ECS	ECS services should be attached to a load balancer	Compliance	Medium	Navigate to the ECS console, select your cluster, and either create or update your service by enabling the Load balancer option and choosing an existing Application Load Balancer (ALB) or Network Load Balancer (NLB). Specify the target group during the configuration process and complete the creation or update to ensure traffic is distributed across your task instances. ECS	AWS ECS services should not have public IP addresses assigned to them automatically	Compliance	High	Navigate to the ECS console, select your cluster, and either create or update your service. ECS	ECS task definition containers should not have secrets passed as environment variables	Compliance	High	Store your sensitive data in AWS Secrets Manager by creating a new secret and noting its name or ARN. Then, update your task definition in the ECS console to reference the secret in the Secrets section instead of using environment variables. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonECS/latest/developerguide/specifying-sensitive-data.html	
ECS	ECS containers should run as non-privileged	Compliance	High	Update your task definition in the ECS console and specify a non-root user ID or username in the User field of the container definition. This configuration minimizes security risks by limiting permissions within the container. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/config/latest/developerguide/ecs-containers-nonprivileged.html	
ECS	ECS containers should be limited to read-only access to root filesystems	Compliance	High	Update your task definition in the ECS console and enable the readonlyRootfs option by setting it to true. This configuration prevents any modifications to the filesystem, enhancing the security of the container environment. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/config/latest/developerguide/ecs-containers-readonly-access.html	
ECS	ECS task definitions should have logging enabled	Compliance	Medium	Update your task definition in the ECS console and create a new revision. In the container definition, select awslogs as the log driver under the Log configuration section, specifying the log group and stream prefix for Amazon CloudWatch Logs. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonECS/latest/developerguide/ecs-logging-monitoring.html	
ECS	ECS task definitions should not share the host's process namespace	Compliance	High	Update your task definition in the ECS console and create a new revision. Set the PID mode to task or leave it blank to prevent the container from accessing the host's processes, enhancing security. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/securityhub/latest/userguide/ecs-controls.html	
ECS	ECS task definitions should not use root user.	Compliance	High	Update your task definition in the ECS console and specify a non-root user ID or username in the User field of the container definition. This enhances security by reducing the risk of privilege escalation within the container. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/config/latest/developerguide/ecs-task-definition-nonroot-user.html	
ECS	ECS task definition container definitions should be checked for host mode	Compliance	High	Go to the AWS Management Console, select your ECS cluster, navigate to the Task Definitions section, and review the container definitions for the networkMode setting. If its set to host, the container will share the host's network stack, allowing for direct access to host ports Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/config/latest/developerguide/ecs-task-definition-user-for-host-mode-check.html

RDS	RDS database instances should use a custom administrator username	Compliance	High	To set a custom administrator username for your RDS DB instances, log into the AWS Management Console, navigate to the RDS dashboard, and create a new instance. During the creation process, specify your custom username in the DB instance identifier section. If you have existing instances, you may need to create a new instance and migrate data or change the existing username as per your requirements https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/UserGuide/Welcome.html	Cost: None/$0 
RDS	RDS DB instances should not use public subnet	Compliance	Low	To ensure that your RDS instances do not use public subnets, check the subnet configuration when creating the instance. Log into the AWS Management Console, navigate to the VPC dashboard, and verify that the selected subnet for your RDS instance is private. If needed, launch a new RDS instance in a private subnet https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/UserGuide/USER_VPC.html	Cost: None/$0 
RDS	RDS PostgreSQL DB instances should not be exposed to local file read vulnerability	Compliance	Low	To protect RDS PostgreSQL instances from local file read vulnerabilities, ensure that the appropriate configurations are set. Verify that the local_file setting is disabled in your instance parameters. Log into the AWS Management Console, navigate to the RDS dashboard, select your PostgreSQL instance, and modify the DB parameter group settings  https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/UserGuide/Welcome.html	Cost: None/$0 
RDS	RDS DB instances should prohibit public access	Compliance	High	To prohibit public access for RDS DB instances, log into the AWS Management Console and navigate to the RDS dashboard. Select your DB instance and ensure that the "Public accessibility" option is set to No. Save changes and apply them either immediately or during the next maintenance window https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/UserGuide/Welcome.html	Cost: None/$0 
RDS	RDS DB instance should be protected by backup plan	Compliance	Low	To protect your RDS DB instances with a backup plan, ensure that automated backups are enabled. Log into the AWS Management Console, select your RDS instance, and click on Modify. Ensure that the Backup retention period is greater than 0 days, and apply the changes immediately or during the next maintenance window https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/UserGuide/Welcome.html	Cost: None/$0 
RDS	An RDS event notifications subscription should be configured for critical database parameter group events	Compliance	Low	To configure an RDS event notifications subscription for critical database parameter group events, log into the AWS Management Console, navigate to the RDS dashboard, and select "Event subscriptions." Create a new subscription and select the parameter group events you wish to monitor. Specify the notification method, such as an SNS topic. https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/UserGuide/USER_Events.html#USER_Events.Subscribing	Cost: None/$0 
RDS	An RDS event notifications subscription should be configured for critical database security group events	Compliance	Medium	RDS event notifications subscription for critical database security group events, log into the AWS Management Console, navigate to the RDS dashboard, and select "Event subscriptions." Create a new subscription by selecting the security group events you want to monitor, and specify the notification method (e.g., an SNS topic). https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/UserGuide/USER_Events.html#USER_Events.Subscribing 	Cost: None/$0 
RDS	RDS DB snapshots should be encrypted at rest	Compliance	High	RDS DB snapshots are encrypted at rest, create snapshots with encryption enabled. Log into the AWS Management Console, navigate to your RDS instance, and select "Take snapshot." Ensure that the "Enable encryption" option is selected. For existing unencrypted snapshots, you can create a copy of the snapshot with encryption enabled https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/UserGuide/Overview.Encryption.html	Cost: None/$0 
RDS	RDS snapshots should prohibit public access	Compliance	High	RDS snapshots, log into the AWS Management Console and navigate to the RDS dashboard. Select the snapshot you wish to modify and ensure that it is set to Private under the Permissions settings. If public access is enabled, modify the snapshot settings accordingly https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/UserGuide/Welcome.html	Cost: None/$0

S3	S3 access points should have block public access settings enabled	Compliance	High	In the S3 Console, create or modify an access point and ensure all "Block public access" options are checked. Open Amazon S3, select "Access Points," choose the desired access point, click "Edit" in "Public access settings," enable "Block all public access," and click "Save changes."	Cost: None/$0 
S3	S3 buckets access control lists (ACLs) should not be used to manage user access to buckets	Compliance	High	Remove any existing ACLs from your S3 buckets and implement IAM policies to manage user access permissions by attaching them to the relevant IAM users or roles.  Go to the bucket's Permissions tab, edit the Access Control List (ACL), uncheck or remove all grantees, and save changes. Then, create an IAM policy under the IAM service, attach it to the relevant IAM users or roles, and manage S3 access permissions through that policy. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/IAM/latest/UserGuide/reference_policies_examples_s3_rw-bucket.html	Cost: None/$0 
S3	S3 bucket cross-region replication should be enabled	Compliance	Medium	Open the S3 Console, select the bucket, go to Management, add a replication rule, specify the destination bucket, enable versioning, and save changes. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/replication.html	Depends on data transfer and storage costs
S3	S3 bucket default encryption should be enabled	Compliance	High	Open the S3 console, select the bucket, go to Properties, enable Default Encryption, and save changes. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/UsingEncryption.html	Cost: None/$0  (but KMS may incur costs)
S3	S3 bucket default encryption should be enabled with KMS	Compliance	High	To enable default encryption with KMS for an S3 bucket, open the S3 console, select the bucket, navigate to the "Properties" tab, enable default encryption, choose "AWS Key Management Service key (SSE-KMS)," select your KMS key, and save the changes. Reference:  https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/example-bucket-policies.html#example-bucket-policies-encryption	KMS costs apply based on usage
S3	S3 buckets should enforce SSL	Compliance	High	To enforce SSL for your S3 buckets, set a bucket policy that denies HTTP requests, allowing only HTTPS. Consider using Amazon CloudFront to require HTTPS and enable server-side encryption for added security. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/example-bucket-policies.html#example-bucket-policies-HTTP-HTTPS	Cost: None/$0 
S3	S3 buckets should have event notifications enabled	Compliance	Medium	Enable S3 bucket event notifications to monitor changes like object creation or deletion by configuring alerts to trigger actions in SNS, SQS, or Lambda. Open the S3 console, select your bucket, go to the Properties tab, and under Event notifications, click Create event notification to specify events like object creation or deletion and choose a destination (SNS, SQS, or Lambda). Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/enable-event-notifications.html	Cost: None/$0  (but may incur SNS costs if used)
S3	S3 buckets should have lifecycle policies configured	Compliance	Medium	Configure S3 lifecycle policies to transition active data to Standard-IA after 30 days, archive to Glacier after 90 days, and delete objects older than 365 days; for archival data, move to Glacier after 90 days and delete after 7 years; for temporary files, delete after 7 days. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/lifecycle-configuration-examples.html	Cost: None/$0 
S3	S3 bucket logging should be enabled	Compliance	High	To enable S3 bucket logging and track access requests, go to the S3 console, select your bucket, click on "Properties," under "Server access logging," enable it, and specify a target bucket to store the logs for analysis. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/enable-server-access-logging.html	Depends on log storage
S3	Ensure MFA Delete is enabled on S3 buckets	Compliance	High	Enable versioning on your S3 bucket through the AWS Management Console, CLI, or SDKs. Then, set up MFA for your IAM user and configure MFA Delete using the AWS CLI or SDKs, as it cannot be done via the Management Console. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/MultiFactorAuthenticationDelete.html	Cost: None/$0 
S3	S3 bucket ACLs should not be accessible to all authenticated user	Compliance	High	To restrict S3 bucket ACLs from being accessible to all authenticated users, remove any permissions for "Authenticated Users" in the ACL settings and review the bucket policy to ensure no access is granted to this group. Consider using bucket policies for more granular control instead of ACLs.reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/walkthrough1.html	Cost: None/$0 
S3	S3 bucket object lock should be enabled	Compliance	Medium	while reating a new bucket and select Enable Object Lock during the setup, choosing the desired retention period and mode. Object Lock cannot be added to existing buckets, so you'll need to migrate objects to a newly created bucket with this feature. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/object-lock-configure.html	Cost: None/$0  (but may incur storage costs)
S3	S3 buckets object logging should be enabled	Compliance	High	To enable object logging for an S3 bucket, go to the bucket in the S3 console, navigate to the Properties tab, and enable Server Access Logging by specifying a target bucket for logs. This will capture and store logs of all requests made to the bucket. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/enable-server-access-logging.html	Depends on log storage
S3	S3 bucket policy should prohibit public access	Compliance	High	To prohibit public access to an S3 bucket, create a bucket policy that denies access to any principal (user or account) except for specific allowed users. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/access-control-block-public-access.html	Cost: None/$0 
S3	AWS S3 permissions granted to other AWS accounts in bucket policies should be restricted	Compliance	Medium	Open bucket polacies, Review Current Policies and Restrict access only to trusted AWS accounts. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/access-grants-cross-accounts.html	Cost: None/$0 
S3	S3 buckets should prohibit public read access	Compliance	High	To prohibit public read access to an S3 bucket, enable all options under the Block public access settings in the bucket's Permissions tab. Additionally, review the bucket policy for any statements allowing public read access and remove or modify them as necessary. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/config/latest/developerguide/s3-bucket-public-read-prohibited.html	Cost: None/$0 
S3	S3 buckets should prohibit public write access	Compliance	High	Access the S3 console, select the bucket, enable all options under Block public access in the Permissions tab, and review the bucket policy to modify or remove any public write access statements as needed. reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/config/latest/developerguide/s3-bucket-public-write-prohibited.html	Cost: None/$0 
S3	S3 buckets static website hosting should be disabled	Compliance	Low	Go to the AWS S3 console, select the desired bucket, and navigate to the "Properties" tab. Scroll down to the "Static website hosting" section, click "Edit," select "Disable," and save the changes.	Cost: None/$0 
S3	S3 buckets with versioning enabled should have lifecycle policies configured	Compliance	Medium	Go to the S3 console, select the bucket, and navigate to the "Management" tab to create a lifecycle rule. Define transitions or expirations for non-current versions, then review and save the rule. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/how-to-set-lifecycle-configuration-intro.html	Cost: None/$0 
S3	S3 bucket versioning should be enabled	Compliance	High	Go to the AWS S3 console, select the bucket, and navigate to the "Properties" tab. In the "Bucket Versioning" section, click "Edit," enable versioning, and save the changes. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/Versioning.html	Cost: None/$0  (but may incur storage costs)
S3	S3 public access should be blocked at account level	Compliance	High	Ggo to the AWS Management Console, open the S3 service, and click on "Block Public Access settings for this account." Then, enable the block for all public access settings, including new and existing buckets, and save the changes to apply account-wide. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/config/latest/developerguide/s3-account-level-public-access-blocks.html	Cost: None/$0 
S3	S3 public access should be blocked at bucket levels	Compliance	Medium	Go to the AWS S3 console, select the bucket, and navigate to the "Permissions" tab. Under the "Block public access" section, click "Edit," enable all block options, and save the changes. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/configuring-block-public-access-bucket.html	Cost: None/$0 
S3	S3 public access should be blocked at account and bucket levels	Compliance	High	Go to the AWS S3 console and navigate to "Block Public Access settings for this account" under the "S3" dashboard. Enable all options to block public access at the account level. Then, for each bucket, go to the "Permissions" tab, edit the "Block public access" settings, enable all options, and save the changes.	Cost: None/$0

VPC	VPCs peering connection should not be allowed in cross account	Compliance	Medium	To disallow VPC peering connections across AWS accounts, ensure that you do not create or accept any peering requests between VPCs in different accounts, implement strict IAM policies that restrict permissions for VPC peering actions, use service control policies (SCPs) in AWS Organizations to deny VPC peering actions across accounts, and regularly audit your VPC settings to identify any unauthorized peering connections. VPC	VPCs peering connection route tables should have least privilege	Compliance	Low	Open the AWS Management Console, navigate to the VPC Dashboard, and select Route Tables to ensure private subnets do not have routes directing traffic to the Internet Gateway (IGW), while public subnets should have a route for 0.0.0.0/0 to the IGW. Then, configure security groups and network ACLs for private subnets to deny unwanted inbound traffic from the Internet and verify the subnet CIDR blocks for proper access restrictions. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/vpc/latest/userguide/VPC_Route_Tables.html	Cost: None/$0 
VPC	VPC route table should restrict public access to IGW	Compliance	Low	To restrict public access, remove any route in the VPC route table pointing to the Internet Gateway (IGW) with 0.0.0.0/0 (IPv4) or ::/0 (IPv6). Then, add necessary private routes for internal access, such as via a NAT Gateway, and verify that no public routes remain. Reference: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/vpc/latest/userguide/route-table-options.html	Cost: None/$0

VPC	VPCs should have both public and private subnets configured	Compliance	Medium	To configure both public and private subnets in a VPC using the AWS Console, create subnets within your VPC and associate a route table with an Internet Gateway (IGW) for the public subnets. Replace any certificates with a key length less than 2,048 bits. https://docs.aws.amazon.com/acm/latest/userguide/acm-certificate.html	Cost: None/$0 
IAM	IAM groups, users, and roles should not have any inline policies	Compliance	High	IAM groups, users, and roles should not have any inline policies: 1. Review the IAM configurations for groups, users, and roles. 2. Replace inline policies with managed policies where possible. https://docs.aws.amazon.com/IAM/latest/UserGuide/access_policies.html	Cost: None/$0 
ACM	ACM certificates should not expire within 30 days	Security	High	Ensure ACM certificates are renewed well before expiration to maintain secure connections. Steps: 1. Monitor certificate expiration dates via ACM. 2. Set up notifications for certificates expiring within 30 days.	
ACM	ACM certificates should not use wildcard certificates	Security	Medium	Avoid using wildcard certificates for better security and specific domain coverage. Steps: 1. Ensure that all certificates are domain-specific and not using wildcards.	
ACM	Ensure that ACM certificates are not in failed state	Security	High	Regularly monitor ACM certificates for any failed validation or provisioning. Steps: 1. Use the ACM console or CLI to check the status of certificates. 2. Resolve any failed certificates promptly.	
ACM	Ensure that ACM certificates are not in pending validation state	Compliance	Medium	Ensure that all certificates are validated promptly and are no longer in the pending validation state. Steps: 1. Check ACM for any certificates in pending validation state. 2. Complete the validation process.	
ACM	Ensure that all the expired ACM certificates are removed	Compliance	Medium	Remove expired certificates to prevent unauthorized usage or security risks. Steps: 1. Use ACM or AWS CLI to identify and remove expired certificates. 2. Implement automated clean-up procedures.	
ACM	RSA certificates managed by ACM should use a key length of at least 2,048 bits	Security	High	Ensure that all RSA certificates use at least 2,048-bit key length for improved security. Steps: 1. Review key lengths of RSA certificates in ACM. 2. Replace certificates with shorter key lengths.	
API Gateway	API Gateway methods authorizer should be configured	Security	High	Ensure API methods are secured by configuring an authorizer (e.g., Lambda authorizer, Cognito user pools, IAM). Steps: 1. Go to the API Gateway console. 2. Configure an authorizer for each method.	
API Gateway	API Gateway methods request parameter should be validated	Security	High	Validate request parameters to protect against invalid or malicious inputs. Steps: 1. Use the API Gateway console to enable request validation on method request parameters.

EventBridge	EventBridge custom event buses should have a resource-based policy attached	Security	High	Ensure that EventBridge custom event buses have a resource-based policy attached to control access. Steps: 1. In the EventBridge Console, navigate to the event buses section. 2. Attach a resource-based policy to the custom event bus to control permissions and access. Link: AWS Documentation on EventBridge resource-based policies

Navigate to the AWS Glue Console. 2. Enable encryption for the connection passwords in the Glue data catalog settings. Link: AWS Glue Data Catalog Encryption

In the Glue Console, navigate to the Data Catalog settings. 2. Enable metadata encryption to ensure data is protected at rest. Link: AWS Glue Encryption of Metadata

Go to the GuardDuty Console. 2. Enable Centralized GuardDuty to configure the detector in all regions. Link: GuardDuty Centralized Configuration	
GuardDuty	GuardDuty should be enabled	Security	High	Ensure that GuardDuty is enabled in all accounts and regions to detect malicious activity. Steps: 1. In the GuardDuty Console, verify that the service is enabled in each region. 2. Enable GuardDuty in any inactive regions. Link: How to Enable GuardDuty	
IAM	Ensure inline policies attached to IAM users, roles, and groups should not allow blocked actions on KMS keys	Security	High	Ensure that inline policies attached to IAM users, roles, and groups do not allow blocked actions on KMS keys. Steps: 1. Review inline policies for IAM entities in the IAM Console. 2. Remove or modify any policies that grant blocked actions on KMS keys. Link: Blocked Actions on KMS Keys	
IAM	IAM groups, users, and roles should not have any inline policies	Security	High	Avoid the use of inline policies attached directly to IAM users, groups, or roles, as they can lead to security misconfigurations. Steps: 1. Review IAM roles, users, and groups for any inline policies. 2. Replace them with managed policies where possible. Link: Best Practices for Managing IAM Policies	
KMS	KMS CMK rotation should be enabled	Security	High	Enable automatic key rotation for your Customer Managed Keys (CMKs) to enhance key security. Steps: 1. In the KMS Console, select your CMK. 2. Enable automatic key rotation. Link: KMS Key Rotation	
KMS	KMS key decryption should be restricted in IAM customer managed policy	Security	High	Restrict KMS key decryption actions in IAM customer managed policies to prevent unauthorized access. Steps: 1. Review IAM policies to ensure they restrict decryption access to the KMS keys based on principle of least privilege. 2. Modify IAM policies to restrict these permissions.	
KMS	KMS key decryption should be restricted in IAM inline policy	Security	High	Restrict KMS key decryption actions in IAM inline policies to prevent unauthorized decryption access. Steps: 1. Review IAM inline policies attached to roles and users. 2. Modify or remove policies that grant KMS decryption access where not required.	
KMS	KMS key should be in use	Operational	High	Ensure that KMS keys are actively in use for encryption purposes. Steps: 1. Check the Key usage history in the KMS Console. 2. If keys are not in use, consider rotating or deactivating them.	
KMS	KMS keys should not be pending deletion	Security	High	Avoid leaving KMS keys in a pending deletion state, as it can cause issues with key access. Steps: 1. In the KMS Console, check for keys in the pending deletion state. 2. Cancel the pending deletion if the key is still required.

VPC	Ensure no security groups allow ingress from ::/0 to remote server administration ports	Security	High	Ensure security groups do not allow remote access to sensitive ports from anywhere (::/0). Steps: 1. Review security group rules. 2. Remove any rules that allow ingress to administration ports (e.g., 22, 3389) from 0.0.0.0/0. Link: VPC Security Group Best Practices	
VPC	Ensure no security groups allow ingress from 0.0.0.0/0 to port 3389	Security	High	Ensure security groups restrict access to port 3389 (RDP) from anywhere (0.0.0.0/0). Steps: 1. Review security group rules. 2. Remove any rules that allow ingress to port 3389 from 0.0.0.0/0. Link: VPC Security Group Best Practices	
VPC	Ensure no security groups allow ingress from 0.0.0.0/0 to remote server administration ports	Security	High	Ensure security groups restrict access to administration ports from anywhere. Steps: 1. Review security group rules for ports like 22 (SSH), 3389 (RDP), etc. 2. Remove any ingress rules allowing access from 0.0.0.0/0. Link: VPC Security Group Best Practices	
VPC	Network ACLs should not allow ingress from 0.0.0.0/0 to port 22 or port 3389	Security	High	Ensure network ACLs do not allow ingress to ports 22 (SSH) or 3389 (RDP) from anywhere. Steps: 1. Review network ACL rules. 2. Modify ACLs to restrict access to these ports. Link: Network ACL Best Practices	
VPC	Security groups should not allow unrestricted access to ports with high risk	Security	High	Restrict access to high-risk ports in your security groups. Steps: 1. Review security group rules for any unrestricted access (0.0.0.0/0) to critical ports. 2. Block or restrict access to ports like 22 (SSH), 3389 (RDP), 3306 (MySQL), etc. Link: Security Group Best Practices	
VPC	Unused EC2 security groups should be removed	Security	High	Remove unused EC2 security groups to reduce potential attack surface. Steps: 1. Identify unused security groups using the AWS Console or CLI. 2. Delete any security groups not associated with running EC2 instances. Link: Managing Security Groups	
VPC	VPC default security group should not allow inbound and outbound traffic	Security	High	Ensure the default VPC security group does not allow unrestricted inbound or outbound traffic. Steps: 1. Review and configure the default security group to deny all inbound/outbound traffic by default. 2. Explicitly allow necessary traffic for security and functionality. Link: Default VPC Security Group	
VPC	VPC EIPs should be associated with an EC2 instance or ENI	Security	High	Ensure Elastic IPs (EIPs) are associated with EC2 instances or Elastic Network Interfaces (ENIs). Steps: 1. VPC	VPC endpoint services should have acceptance required enabled	Security	High	Ensure VPC endpoint services have acceptance required enabled to prevent unauthorized connections. Steps: 1. Review your VPC endpoint service configuration. 2. Enable the acceptance required setting for endpoint services. Link: VPC Endpoint Service Configuration	
VPC	VPC flow logs should be enabled	Security	High	Enable VPC Flow Logs for monitoring network traffic. Steps: 1. Create flow logs for your VPCs, subnets, or ENIs. 2. Send logs to CloudWatch Logs or S3 for analysis and retention. Link: VPC Flow Logs	
VPC	VPC gateway endpoints should restrict public access	Security	High	Ensure VPC gateway endpoints do not allow public access. Steps: 1. Review your VPC gateway endpoint configuration. 2. Set restrict public access to prevent unwanted external traffic. Link: VPC Gateway Endpoints	
VPC	VPC internet gateways should be attached to authorized VPC	Security	High	Ensure VPC internet gateways are only attached to authorized VPCs. Steps: 1. Verify which VPCs are attached to an internet gateway. 2. Detach any internet gateways that are attached to unauthorized or misconfigured VPCs. Link: Internet Gateway Configuration	
VPC	VPC network access control lists (network ACLs) should be associated with a subnet	Security	High	Ensure network ACLs are associated with your subnets for traffic control. Steps: 1. Review NACL associations in your VPC. 2. Associate NACLs with subnets that require traffic control. Link: Network ACLs in VPC	
VPC	VPC route table should restrict public access to IGW	Security	High	Ensure VPC route tables restrict direct access to the internet gateway (IGW) for private subnets. Steps: 1. Review route tables for public and private subnets. 2. Configure the route table to block IGW access for private subnets. Link: VPC Route Tables	
VPC	VPC security groups should be associated with at least one ENI	Security	High	Ensure VPC security groups are associated with at least one Elastic Network Interface (ENI). Steps: 1. Review the security group associations for your ENIs. 2. Ensure every security group is actively associated with one or more ENIs. Link: VPC Security Groups	
VPC	VPC Security groups should only allow unrestricted incoming traffic for authorized ports	Security	High	Ensure security groups only allow incoming traffic on authorized ports. Steps: 1. Review the security group rules. 2. Restrict unrestricted incoming traffic to authorized ports like HTTP (80) or HTTPS (443). Link: VPC Security Group Rules	
VPC	VPC security groups should restrict ingress access on ports 20, 21, 22, 3306, 3389, 4333 from 0.0.0.0/0	Security	High	Ensure VPC security groups restrict ingress access on high-risk ports (20, 21, 22, 3306, 3389, 4333) from any source IP (0.0.0.0/0). Steps: 1. Review security group rules for unrestricted access to these ports. 2. Modify rules to restrict access from any source (0.0.0.0/0). Link: Security Group Best Practices	
VPC	VPC security groups should restrict ingress CIFS access from 0.0.0.0/0 and ::/0	Security	High	Ensure security groups restrict CIFS (port 445) access from any source IP (0.0.0.0/0). Steps: 1. Review security groups for CIFS (port 445) access. 2. Modify rules to restrict ingress from any source. Link: CIFS Security Best Practices	
VPC	VPC security groups should restrict ingress from 0.0.0.0/0 or ::/0 to Cassandra ports 7199 or 9160 or 8888	Security	High	Ensure security groups restrict access to Cassandra ports (7199, 9160, 8888) from any source IP (0.0.0.0/0 or ::/0). Steps: 1. Review security group rules for Cassandra ports. 2. Restrict access to these ports to authorized sources only. Link: VPC Security Group Best Practices	
WAFv2	A WAFV2 web ACL should have at least one rule or rule group	Security	High	Ensure that your WAFv2 web ACL has at least one rule or rule group to protect your application from malicious web traffic. Steps: 1. In the AWS Management Console, navigate to AWS WAF. 2. Create a new web ACL or update an existing one. 3. Add at least one rule or rule group to the web ACL. You can choose AWS Managed Rules or custom rules depending on your security needs. Link: AWS WAFv2 - Web ACLs and Rules	
WAFv2	Logging should be enabled on AWS WAFv2 regional and global web access control list (ACLs)	Security	High	Enable logging on your WAFv2 web ACLs to capture detailed information about the web traffic being blocked or allowed. This helps with monitoring and debugging. Steps: 1. Go to AWS WAF in the AWS Management Console. 2. For each web ACL, enable logging. 3. Choose the CloudWatch Logs group to store the log data or configure it to send to Amazon S3. Link: AWS WAFv2 - Logging Configuration	
RDS	RDS DB instance automatic minor version upgrade should be enabled	Security	High	Recommendation: Ensure that the automatic minor version upgrade setting is enabled for all RDS DB instances to ensure that your database instances are kept up-to-date with the latest minor version of the database engine. Enabling this setting allows RDS to automatically upgrade the instance during the maintenance window, reducing the risk of security vulnerabilities and performance issues related to outdated versions.  Steps/Approach: Open the Amazon RDS console. In the navigation pane, choose Databases. Select the DB instance to modify. Under the Maintenance & backups section, ensure the Auto minor version upgrade option is set to Yes. If it is not enabled, choose Modify to edit the DB instance. Under the Maintenance & backups section, check the box for Auto minor version upgrade. Apply the changes immediately or during the next maintenance window based on your preference. Source: AWS RDS Documentation - Modify DB Instance Amazon RDS Best Practices	
S3	Ensure all data in AWS S3 has been discovered, classified and secured when required	Security	High	Recommendation: Recommendation: Implement AWS S3 data discovery and classification policies, along with encryption, access control, and monitoring to ensure that all S3 data is properly classified and secured. Fix Steps: Data Discovery:  Enable Amazon Macie to automatically discover, classify, and protect sensitive data in S3. Macie uses machine learning to discover and classify sensitive data like personally identifiable information (PII). Enable AWS Config to track changes in the S3 buckets and ensure that data classification is updated as required. Data Classification:  Use S3 Object Tags and S3 Inventory reports to classify data according to business needs. Tags can be used to categorize S3 objects based on the content, sensitivity, or other criteria. Ensure that Macie or custom solutions are used to classify data based on predefined rules for sensitive data (e.g., PII, PCI). Securing Data:  Enable S3 Bucket Encryption using AWS KMS (Key Management Service) to automatically encrypt data at rest. Implement S3 Block Public Access to restrict public access to your S3 buckets and objects, preventing unintended exposure. Use IAM policies and S3 access control lists (ACLs) to enforce least privilege access to S3 data. Enable S3 Versioning to keep track of object changes and maintain data integrity. Implement AWS CloudTrail to monitor and log all S3 bucket access requests for auditing and security. Ongoing Monitoring:  Continuously monitor your S3 buckets using Amazon GuardDuty for unusual access patterns or malicious activities. Configure AWS CloudWatch to set alarms based on specific S3 activity (e.g., access from unusual locations). Link to AWS Documentation: Amazon Macie Documentation Amazon S3 Security Best Practices AWS Key Management Service (KMS) Documentation AWS CloudTrail Documentation AWS Config Documentation
